### Section: 7.1 Importance of Parks and Open Space:

Parks and open space play a crucial role in the urban environment, providing a variety of benefits to both the community and the ecosystem. In this section, we will explore the importance of parks and open space in Foshan, China, and how they contribute to the overall well-being of the city.

#### 7.1a Benefits of Parks and Open Space in Urban Areas

Parks and open space in urban areas offer a multitude of benefits, both to the community and the environment. These benefits can be categorized into four main areas: recreation, ecology, aesthetic value, and positive health impacts.

##### Recreational Benefits

One of the most well-known benefits of parks and open space is their role in providing recreational opportunities for the community. Urban open space is often appreciated for the recreational activities it offers, such as organized sports, individual exercise, and passive recreation. Research has shown that when open spaces are attractive and accessible, people are more likely to engage in physical activity. This is especially important in urban areas where sedentary lifestyles are becoming increasingly prevalent. Time spent in an urban open space for recreation offers a reprieve from the urban environment and a break from over-stimulation. Additionally, studies have shown that coupling physical activities with green space environments leads to decreased levels of stress, lowered risk for depression, and increased frequency of exercise.

##### Ecological Benefits

The conservation of nature in an urban environment has direct impact on people for another reason as well. As humans live more and more in man-made surroundings, the importance of preserving natural spaces becomes increasingly apparent. Urban open spaces serve as islands of nature, promoting biodiversity and providing a home for natural species in environments that are otherwise uninhabitable due to city development. This not only benefits the ecosystem, but also provides a sense of balance and harmony for the community.

##### Aesthetic Value

Parks and open space also contribute to the aesthetic value of a city. The natural beauty and tranquility of these spaces offer a contrast to the bustling urban environment, providing a sense of calm and relaxation. This is especially important in Foshan, where the city's rapid urban development has led to a loss of traditional Chinese landscapes. Parks and open space help to preserve and showcase these landscapes, adding to the cultural and aesthetic appeal of the city.

##### Positive Health Impacts

Finally, parks and open space have been shown to have positive health impacts on the community. Studies have shown that access to green spaces can improve mental health, reduce stress, and increase overall well-being. In Foshan, where air pollution is a major concern, parks and open space offer a breath of fresh air and a chance to connect with nature. This can have a significant impact on the health of the community, especially for those living in urban areas where access to green spaces may be limited.

In conclusion, parks and open space are essential components of urban planning and development. They offer a multitude of benefits to the community and the environment, and are crucial for creating a livable and sustainable city. In the following sections, we will explore the various types of parks and open space in Foshan, and how they contribute to the overall urban environment.





### Related Context
```
# Urban forestry

### China

#### Urban Green Space Development

With a rapidly growing population, China has started developing strategies to improve urban life. The concept "making forests enter cities and making cities embrace forests" has been promoted. The creation of the "National Forest City" title in 2004 has incentivized urban forest development. This program has led to significant positive changes in the quality and quantity of many Chinese cities. Currently, 58 cities have been awarded this title. While changes have been made, inequity of recreational green spaces may still be a challenge. In a case study of Wuhan, China, equal distribution of greenspaces was found, but there was unequal distribution of public parks. These findings suggest that some social groups and populations cannot equally enjoy the recreational and health benefits of these public greenspaces.

#### Nanjing

Nanjing Vertical Forest Project, designed by Stefano Boeri of Stefano Boeri Architetti, consists of two towers: one 200 meter tower that will hold office spaces, a museum, a rooftop club, and a green architecture school while the other 108-meter tower that will include a Hyatt hotel and swimming pool. With construction now complete, native trees, shrubs, and perennials are being installed. 600 tall trees, 200 medium-sized trees and 2,500 cascading plants and shrubs will be planted on the building facades. It is expected to absorb 18 tonnes of <CO2> while providing 16,5 tonnes of oxygen annually.

#### Shanghai

A 99 km long and 100 m wide forest belt surrounding the city was completed in 2003. The heat island issue has been significantly reduced.

Another pilot project by Shanghai Municipal Agricultural Commission aims to convert 35% of the total area of Shanghai to urban forest. A forest network of two rings, eight lines, five zones, multi-corridors, multi-grids, and one chain was introduced in the project, which means planting two ring-shaped forests, an inner ring 500 m wide by
```

#### 7.1a Benefits of Parks and Open Space in Urban Areas

Parks and open space in urban areas offer a multitude of benefits, both to the community and the environment. These benefits can be categorized into four main areas: recreation, ecology, aesthetic value, and positive health impacts.

##### Recreational Benefits

One of the most well-known benefits of parks and open space is their role in providing recreational opportunities for the community. Urban open space is often appreciated for the recreational activities it offers, such as organized sports, individual exercise, and passive recreation. Research has shown that when open spaces are attractive and accessible, people are more likely to engage in physical activity. This is especially important in urban areas where sedentary lifestyles are becoming increasingly prevalent. Time spent in an urban open space for recreation offers a reprieve from the urban environment and a break from over-stimulation. Additionally, studies have shown that coupling physical activities with green space environments leads to decreased levels of stress, lowered risk for depression, and increased frequency of exercise.

##### Ecological Benefits

The conservation of nature in an urban environment has direct impact on people for another reason as well. As humans live more and more in man-made surroundings, the importance of preserving natural spaces becomes increasingly apparent. Urban open spaces serve as islands of nature, promoting biodiversity and providing a home for natural species in environments that are otherwise uninhabitable due to city development. This not only benefits the ecosystem, but also contributes to the overall health and well-being of the community.

##### Aesthetic Value

Parks and open space also play a crucial role in enhancing the aesthetic value of urban areas. They provide a sense of beauty and tranquility in the midst of a bustling city. The use of landscaping and natural elements in parks can also add to the overall aesthetic appeal of a city. This is especially important in China, where there is a growing appreciation for natural and traditional elements in urban design.

##### Positive Health Impacts

In addition to the physical and mental health benefits of recreation, parks and open space also have a positive impact on public health. Studies have shown that access to green spaces can improve mental health, reduce stress, and increase overall well-being. This is especially important in urban areas where there is a high prevalence of mental health issues and stress-related disorders. By providing accessible and attractive parks and open space, cities can promote a healthier and happier community.

### Conclusion

Parks and open space are essential components of urban planning and development. They offer a multitude of benefits, both to the community and the environment. As cities continue to grow and evolve, it is crucial to prioritize the development and maintenance of parks and open space to create livable and sustainable urban environments. 





### Subsection: 7.2a Principles of Park Design

Park design is a crucial aspect of urban planning and development. It involves creating a plan for the layout, features, and management of a park. The design process is influenced by various factors, including the intended purpose and audience of the park, as well as the available land features.

#### 7.2a.1 Principles of Park Design

The design of a park is guided by several principles that aim to create a functional and aesthetically pleasing space. These principles include:

1. **Functionality**: The park should serve its intended purpose. For instance, a park designed for recreation should include features such as playgrounds, walking paths, and sports facilities.

2. **Accessibility**: The park should be accessible to all members of the community, regardless of their age or physical abilities. This includes providing features such as ramps, handrails, and wide paths.

3. **Sustainability**: The park should be designed and managed in a way that minimizes its environmental impact. This can be achieved through the use of sustainable materials, energy-efficient infrastructure, and conservation of natural resources.

4. **Aesthetics**: The park should be visually appealing and contribute to the overall aesthetic of the surrounding area. This can be achieved through the use of landscaping, architectural features, and artistic elements.

5. **Maintenance**: The park should be designed in a way that is easy to maintain and manage. This includes considering factors such as the type of vegetation, the layout of paths and walkways, and the placement of infrastructure.

#### 7.2a.2 Park Design Process

The process of designing a park typically involves several stages, including:

1. **Conceptualization**: This involves defining the purpose and audience of the park, as well as identifying the key features and design elements.

2. **Planning**: This involves creating a detailed plan for the layout of the park, including the placement of features, infrastructure, and landscaping.

3. **Implementation**: This involves constructing the park according to the design plan.

4. **Maintenance and Management**: This involves ongoing management and maintenance of the park to ensure its functionality and aesthetic appeal.

#### 7.2a.3 Case Studies

To further illustrate the principles and process of park design, let's look at two case studies: the Nanjing Vertical Forest Project and the Shanghai Urban Forest Project.

##### Nanjing Vertical Forest Project

The Nanjing Vertical Forest Project, designed by Stefano Boeri of Stefano Boeri Architetti, is a prime example of sustainable park design. The project involves the construction of two towers covered in trees and vegetation, which aim to absorb carbon dioxide and provide oxygen. This project not only serves as a recreational space but also as a model for sustainable urban development.

##### Shanghai Urban Forest Project

The Shanghai Urban Forest Project, on the other hand, focuses on the creation of a forest belt surrounding the city. This project aims to reduce the heat island effect and improve the overall aesthetic of the city. The project involves the planting of trees and vegetation along a 99 km long and 100 m wide belt, which will be managed by the Shanghai Municipal Agricultural Commission.

These case studies demonstrate the importance of considering sustainability and functionality in park design. They also highlight the role of urban forestry in improving the quality of life in cities.




### Subsection: 7.2b Sustainable Park Management Practices

Sustainable park management practices are essential for ensuring the long-term viability and benefits of parks. These practices aim to balance the needs of the park with the needs of the surrounding community and the environment. They also aim to ensure that the park continues to provide benefits to the community in the future.

#### 7.2b.1 Sustainable Park Management Principles

Sustainable park management is guided by several principles that aim to create a balance between the needs of the park and the needs of the surrounding community and environment. These principles include:

1. **Sustainability**: The management of the park should aim to minimize its environmental impact and ensure its long-term viability. This can be achieved through the use of sustainable practices, such as energy-efficient infrastructure, conservation of natural resources, and the use of sustainable materials.

2. **Community Engagement**: The management of the park should involve the local community. This can be achieved through community involvement in decision-making processes, volunteer programs, and educational initiatives.

3. **Economic Viability**: The management of the park should aim to ensure its economic viability. This can be achieved through the generation of revenue from activities such as park entry fees, rentals, and events.

4. **Resilience**: The management of the park should aim to build its resilience to potential threats, such as climate change, natural disasters, and changes in community needs.

#### 7.2b.2 Sustainable Park Management Practices

The management of a park involves a range of practices that aim to achieve the principles of sustainable park management. These practices include:

1. **Sustainable Landscape Management**: This involves the use of sustainable landscape practices, such as the use of native vegetation, water conservation, and the use of sustainable materials.

2. **Sustainable Infrastructure Management**: This involves the management of the park's infrastructure in a way that minimizes its environmental impact and ensures its long-term viability. This can be achieved through the use of sustainable materials, energy-efficient infrastructure, and the implementation of renewable energy sources.

3. **Community Engagement and Education**: This involves engaging the local community in the management of the park and providing education about the park's benefits and management practices.

4. **Monitoring and Evaluation**: This involves monitoring and evaluating the park's performance to identify areas for improvement and ensure the effectiveness of management practices.

5. **Adaptive Management**: This involves adapting management practices in response to changes in the park's environment, community needs, or other factors.

By implementing these sustainable park management practices, parks can continue to provide benefits to the community in the future while minimizing their environmental impact.

### Conclusion

In conclusion, the design and management of parks in urban areas is a complex and multifaceted process. It requires careful consideration of various factors such as the local environment, community needs, and sustainability. By understanding these factors and implementing effective management practices, parks can serve as valuable spaces for recreation, relaxation, and community building. They can also contribute to the overall livability and quality of life in urban areas.

## Chapter 8: Transportation:




### Introduction

Foshan, a bustling city in southern China, is home to a complex and ever-evolving transportation system. This chapter will delve into the intricacies of Foshan's transportation systems and networks, providing a comprehensive guide to understanding and navigating this urban landscape.

The transportation system in Foshan is a critical component of the city's urban planning and development. It is designed to facilitate the movement of people and goods, and to connect the city with other urban centers both within and outside of China. The system is composed of a variety of modes, including road, rail, water, and air transportation, each with its own unique characteristics and challenges.

In this chapter, we will explore the history and evolution of Foshan's transportation system, examining how it has been shaped by factors such as population growth, economic development, and technological advancements. We will also delve into the planning and management of the system, discussing the strategies and policies that guide its operation and development.

Furthermore, we will examine the impact of the transportation system on the city's urban fabric and quality of life. We will discuss how the system influences the spatial organization of the city, shaping its physical form and social dynamics. We will also explore the environmental and social implications of the system, considering its impact on air quality, noise levels, and community cohesion.

Finally, we will look to the future, discussing the challenges and opportunities that lie ahead for Foshan's transportation system. We will consider how the system can be improved and expanded to meet the needs of a growing and changing city, and how it can be integrated with other aspects of urban planning and development.

This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive and accessible guide to Foshan's transportation systems and networks. Whether you are a resident of the city, a visitor, or a professional in the field of urban planning and development, we hope that this chapter will enhance your understanding and appreciation of this vital aspect of Foshan's urban landscape.




### Subsection: 8.1a Modes of Transportation in Foshan

Foshan, like many other cities in China, has a complex and diverse transportation system. The city is served by a variety of modes of transportation, each with its own unique characteristics and challenges. In this section, we will provide an overview of the different modes of transportation in Foshan, discussing their history, evolution, and impact on the city's urban fabric.

#### Road Transportation

Road transportation is the most common mode of transportation in Foshan. The city is served by a comprehensive network of roads, including national highways, provincial highways, and urban roads. The road network in Foshan is constantly expanding to meet the growing demand for transportation.

The history of road transportation in Foshan dates back to the early 20th century when the city was connected to other urban centers by a network of dirt roads. However, it was not until the 1950s that the city began to develop a modern road network. The construction of the Guangzhou-Foshan Expressway in the 1990s marked a significant milestone in the development of road transportation in Foshan.

Road transportation plays a crucial role in the city's economy, facilitating the movement of people and goods. It is also a key component of the city's urban planning and development. The expansion of the road network has led to the development of new urban areas, transforming the city's physical form and social dynamics.

#### Rail Transportation

Rail transportation is another important mode of transportation in Foshan. The city is served by a network of railways, including the Guangzhou-Foshan Railway and the Guangzhou-Shenzhen Railway. These railways connect Foshan with other urban centers in Guangdong Province and beyond.

The history of rail transportation in Foshan dates back to the late 19th century when the city was connected to Guangzhou by a narrow-gauge railway. However, it was not until the 1950s that the city began to develop a modern railway network. The construction of the Guangzhou-Foshan Railway in the 1990s marked a significant milestone in the development of rail transportation in Foshan.

Rail transportation is a fast and efficient mode of transportation, making it a popular choice for both commuters and long-distance travelers. It also plays a crucial role in the city's economy, facilitating the movement of goods and people.

#### Water Transportation

Water transportation is a significant mode of transportation in Foshan, particularly for goods transportation. The city is located on the Pearl River, which serves as a major trade route connecting Foshan with other urban centers in Guangdong Province and beyond.

The history of water transportation in Foshan dates back to the early 20th century when the city was connected to other urban centers by a network of canals. However, it was not until the 1950s that the city began to develop a modern water transportation system. The construction of the Pearl River Bridge in the 1990s marked a significant milestone in the development of water transportation in Foshan.

Water transportation is a cost-effective mode of transportation, particularly for goods transportation. It also plays a crucial role in the city's economy, facilitating the movement of goods and people.

#### Air Transportation

Air transportation is a relatively new mode of transportation in Foshan. The city is served by the Foshan Shadi Airport, which provides domestic and international air services.

The history of air transportation in Foshan dates back to the late 1990s when the city began to develop its first airport. The construction of the Foshan Shadi Airport in the early 2000s marked a significant milestone in the development of air transportation in Foshan.

Air transportation is a fast and convenient mode of transportation, particularly for long-distance travelers. It also plays a crucial role in the city's economy, facilitating the movement of people and goods.

In the next section, we will delve deeper into the planning and management of Foshan's transportation system, discussing the strategies and policies that guide its operation and development.




### Subsection: 8.1b Existing Transportation Infrastructure

Foshan's transportation infrastructure is a complex network of roads, railways, and waterways that connect the city with other urban centers in Guangdong Province and beyond. The city's transportation infrastructure is constantly evolving to meet the growing demand for transportation and to support the city's economic development.

#### Road Infrastructure

Foshan's road infrastructure is a comprehensive network of roads, including national highways, provincial highways, and urban roads. The city's road network is constantly expanding to meet the growing demand for transportation. The construction of the Guangzhou-Foshan Expressway in the 1990s marked a significant milestone in the development of road transportation in Foshan.

The road infrastructure in Foshan is not only important for transportation but also plays a crucial role in the city's urban planning and development. The expansion of the road network has led to the development of new urban areas, transforming the city's physical form and social dynamics.

#### Rail Infrastructure

Foshan's rail infrastructure is a network of railways, including the Guangzhou-Foshan Railway and the Guangzhou-Shenzhen Railway. These railways connect Foshan with other urban centers in Guangdong Province and beyond. The history of rail transportation in Foshan dates back to the late 19th century when the city was connected to Guangzhou by a narrow-gauge railway. However, it was not until the 1950s that the city began to develop a modern rail network.

The rail infrastructure in Foshan is a key component of the city's transportation system. It provides a fast and efficient mode of transportation for both passengers and goods. The construction of the Guangzhou-Foshan Railway in the 1990s marked a significant milestone in the development of rail transportation in Foshan.

#### Water Infrastructure

Foshan's water infrastructure is a network of waterways, including the Pearl River and the Beijiang River. The history of water transportation in Foshan dates back to the early 20th century when the city was connected to other urban centers by a network of canals.

The water infrastructure in Foshan is not only important for transportation but also plays a crucial role in the city's economy. The Pearl River and the Beijiang River are important trade routes, facilitating the movement of goods between Foshan and other urban centers. The development of the water infrastructure in Foshan has led to the growth of the city's economy, making it one of the most prosperous cities in China.





### Subsection: 8.2a Case Study: Foshan's Metro System

Foshan's metro system, also known as the Foshan Urban Rail Transit, is a rapid transit system that serves the city of Foshan and its surrounding areas. The system is operated by the Foshan Urban Rail Transit Corporation, a subsidiary of the Guangzhou Metro Corporation. The metro system is a crucial component of Foshan's transportation network, providing a fast and efficient mode of transportation for both passengers and goods.

#### History of Foshan's Metro System

The development of Foshan's metro system can be traced back to the 1990s when the city began to experience rapid economic growth and urbanization. The construction of the Guangzhou-Foshan Railway in 1996 marked a significant milestone in the development of rail transportation in Foshan. However, it was not until the early 2000s that the city began to develop a comprehensive metro system.

The first phase of the Foshan Urban Rail Transit was completed in 2006 and consisted of two lines, Line 1 and Line 2. Line 1 runs from the Guangzhou South Railway Station to the Shunde Railway Station, while Line 2 runs from the Guangzhou East Railway Station to the Foshan West Railway Station. The construction of these lines was funded by a joint venture between the Foshan Municipal Government and the Guangzhou Metro Corporation.

#### Current State of Foshan's Metro System

Today, the Foshan Urban Rail Transit consists of three lines, Line 1, Line 2, and Line 3. Line 1 has been extended to the Shunde Railway Station, while Line 2 has been extended to the Foshan West Railway Station. Line 3, which was completed in 2016, runs from the Guangzhou East Railway Station to the Foshan West Railway Station.

The metro system in Foshan is a fully automated system, with trains operating at a frequency of 2-3 minutes during peak hours. The system is also equipped with a state-of-the-art signaling system, allowing for precise control of train movements and reducing the risk of accidents.

#### Future Developments

The Foshan Urban Rail Transit Corporation has announced plans to expand the metro system to include a fourth line, Line 4, which will run from the Guangzhou East Railway Station to the Foshan West Railway Station. The construction of this line is expected to be completed by 2020.

In addition, the corporation is also considering the development of a monorail system in Foshan. The proposed monorail system would run along the Guangzhou-Foshan Expressway and connect the city with the Guangzhou Baiyun International Airport.

#### Conclusion

Foshan's metro system is a crucial component of the city's transportation network, providing a fast and efficient mode of transportation for both passengers and goods. The system's continuous expansion and modernization reflect the city's commitment to improving its transportation infrastructure and supporting its economic development. 





### Subsection: 8.2b Integrated Transportation Planning in Foshan

Foshan's transportation system is a complex network that includes roads, highways, public transportation, and freight transportation. To effectively plan and improve this network, Foshan has adopted an integrated transportation planning approach. This approach involves the coordination and collaboration of various transportation modes and agencies to develop a comprehensive and sustainable transportation system.

#### The Role of Integrated Transportation Planning in Foshan

Integrated transportation planning plays a crucial role in Foshan's urban planning and development. It allows for the consideration of all transportation modes and their interactions, leading to more efficient and sustainable transportation systems. By involving all stakeholders, including government agencies, the public, and private businesses, integrated transportation planning ensures that the needs and concerns of all parties are addressed.

#### The Process of Integrated Transportation Planning in Foshan

The process of integrated transportation planning in Foshan involves several steps. The first step is to define the goals and objectives of the transportation system, which may include reducing traffic congestion, improving air quality, and promoting sustainable transportation modes. The next step is to identify the transportation needs of the city, including the movement of people and goods. This is done through data collection and analysis, including traffic studies, land use analysis, and public input.

Once the needs have been identified, alternative transportation solutions are developed and evaluated. This may include the construction of new roads, the expansion of public transportation systems, or the implementation of new technologies. The alternatives are then compared based on their effectiveness in meeting the goals and objectives, their cost, and their impact on the environment and the community.

The final step is to develop and implement a transportation plan. This plan may include specific projects, policies, and programs to address the identified transportation needs. It is important for the plan to be flexible and adaptable to changing conditions and needs.

#### Challenges and Solutions for Integrated Transportation Planning in Foshan

Despite its benefits, integrated transportation planning in Foshan faces several challenges. One of the main challenges is the coordination and collaboration of various transportation modes and agencies. This requires effective communication and decision-making processes. To address this challenge, Foshan has established a transportation planning authority that brings together all stakeholders to develop and implement transportation plans.

Another challenge is the lack of funding for transportation projects. To address this, Foshan has implemented a public-private partnership program, where private companies can invest in transportation projects in exchange for a share of the revenue generated. This has helped to fund several transportation projects, including the construction of a new highway and the expansion of the public transportation system.

In conclusion, integrated transportation planning is a crucial aspect of Foshan's urban planning and development. It allows for the consideration of all transportation modes and their interactions, leading to more efficient and sustainable transportation systems. By involving all stakeholders and adopting innovative solutions, Foshan continues to improve its transportation network and address the transportation needs of its growing population.





#### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the various transportation systems and networks that are essential for the development and functioning of a city. We have discussed the different modes of transportation, including road, rail, air, and water, and how they are interconnected to form a comprehensive transportation network. We have also examined the challenges and opportunities that come with the development and management of these systems, and how they impact the overall urban planning and development of a city.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of a well-planned and integrated transportation system in a city. A well-designed transportation network not only facilitates the movement of people and goods, but also promotes economic growth, social equity, and sustainability. It is crucial for urban planners to consider the long-term impacts of transportation systems on the city and its inhabitants, and to prioritize the development of sustainable and equitable transportation options.

Another important aspect to consider is the role of technology in transportation systems. With the rise of smart cities and the Internet of Things, there is a growing potential for the integration of technology into transportation networks. This can lead to more efficient and sustainable transportation options, as well as improved safety and convenience for users. However, it is important for urban planners to carefully consider the potential implications and challenges of implementing technology in transportation systems.

In conclusion, transportation systems and networks play a crucial role in the development and functioning of a city. It is essential for urban planners to carefully consider the design, management, and integration of transportation systems in order to create a sustainable, equitable, and efficient urban environment.

### Introduction

Water is a vital resource for any city, and Foshan is no exception. As one of the largest and most rapidly developing cities in China, Foshan faces significant challenges in managing its water resources. This chapter will provide a comprehensive guide to understanding and addressing these challenges.

The chapter will begin by examining the current state of Foshan's water resources, including the availability and quality of water. It will then delve into the various factors that influence water resource management, such as population growth, urbanization, and climate change. 

Next, the chapter will explore the different approaches and strategies used in water resource management, including water conservation, water reuse, and water pricing. It will also discuss the role of technology and innovation in addressing water scarcity and pollution.

Finally, the chapter will look at the future of water resource management in Foshan, considering the potential impacts of continued development and the need for sustainable practices. It will also discuss the importance of community engagement and education in promoting responsible water use.

By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the challenges and opportunities in water resource management in Foshan. They will also have the knowledge and tools to contribute to the development of sustainable water management practices in the city.




### Section: 9.1 Water Resources in Foshan:

Foshan, like many other cities in China, faces significant challenges in managing its water resources. The city's rapid development and urbanization have put immense pressure on its water resources, leading to over-extraction of groundwater and falling water tables. This has resulted in serious land subsidence and flooding, further exacerbating the city's water scarcity.

#### 9.1a Water Sources and Supply in Foshan

Foshan's water resources are primarily derived from three sources: groundwater, surface water, and imported water. Groundwater is the most significant source, accounting for approximately 60% of the city's water supply. However, over-extraction of groundwater has led to falling water tables and serious land subsidence, particularly in the northern part of the city.

Surface water, primarily from the Pearl River, accounts for about 30% of Foshan's water supply. However, the river's water quality is often poor due to industrial and domestic pollution, limiting its use for drinking water. The city also relies on imported water from neighboring cities and provinces, particularly during periods of drought.

The city's water supply is managed by the Foshan Water Supply and Drainage Bureau, which is responsible for the construction, operation, and maintenance of the city's water infrastructure. The bureau is also responsible for implementing water conservation measures and enforcing water use regulations.

Despite these efforts, Foshan continues to face significant water scarcity. The city's per capita water resources have been declining in recent years, and the city is expected to face even greater water scarcity in the future due to population growth and urbanization.

In the next section, we will explore the various factors that influence water resource management in Foshan, including population growth, urbanization, and climate change.

#### 9.1b Water Quality and Pollution in Foshan

The quality of Foshan's water resources is a significant concern for the city's residents and policymakers. The city's rapid development and industrialization have led to significant pollution of its water resources, particularly the Pearl River. The river's water quality is often poor due to industrial and domestic pollution, limiting its use for drinking water.

The Pearl River is a major source of drinking water for Foshan, accounting for approximately 30% of the city's water supply. However, the river's water quality is often poor due to industrial and domestic pollution. Industrial effluents from textile, paper, and chemical industries, among others, contain a variety of pollutants, including heavy metals, organic pollutants, and microorganisms, which can contaminate the river's water. Domestic wastewater, which is often untreated, also contributes to the river's pollution.

The pollution of the Pearl River has significant implications for Foshan's water resources. The river's pollution not only affects the quality of the city's drinking water but also reduces the availability of clean water for other uses, such as agriculture and industry. This, in turn, can hinder the city's economic development and exacerbate social inequalities.

To address the issue of water pollution, the Foshan Water Supply and Drainage Bureau has implemented a series of measures, including the construction of wastewater treatment plants and the enforcement of stricter regulations on industrial and domestic wastewater discharge. However, these efforts alone may not be sufficient to address the city's water pollution problem.

In the next section, we will explore the role of water pollution in Foshan's water resource management and discuss potential strategies for addressing this issue.

#### 9.1c Water Management Strategies in Foshan

Foshan's water management strategies are designed to address the city's water scarcity and pollution issues. These strategies are implemented by the Foshan Water Supply and Drainage Bureau, which is responsible for the construction, operation, and maintenance of the city's water infrastructure.

One of the key strategies is the promotion of water conservation. The city has implemented a series of measures to encourage water conservation, including the use of water-saving appliances and the implementation of water-saving technologies in industries. The city has also implemented a water pricing policy that aims to encourage water conservation by charging higher prices for water during peak demand periods.

Another important strategy is the development of alternative water sources. The city has been investing in the construction of desalination plants to convert seawater into fresh water. This strategy is particularly important in the context of Foshan's water scarcity, as it provides an additional source of water that is not affected by the city's over-extraction of groundwater.

The city has also been investing in the construction of wastewater treatment plants. These plants aim to treat the city's wastewater to a high standard, making it suitable for reuse in agriculture and industry. This strategy not only helps to reduce the city's water scarcity but also helps to reduce the pollution of the Pearl River.

In addition to these strategies, the city has also been implementing measures to improve the water quality of the Pearl River. These measures include the enforcement of stricter regulations on industrial and domestic wastewater discharge, as well as the construction of pollution control facilities.

Despite these efforts, Foshan continues to face significant water scarcity and pollution issues. The city's water resources are under immense pressure due to its rapid development and urbanization. Therefore, it is crucial for the city to continue to invest in and implement innovative water management strategies to ensure the sustainability of its water resources.

In the next section, we will explore the role of water management in Foshan's urban planning and development.

#### 9.2a Water Pollution Control in Foshan

Water pollution control is a critical aspect of Foshan's water resource management. The city's rapid development and industrialization have led to significant pollution of its water resources, particularly the Pearl River. This pollution not only affects the quality of the city's drinking water but also reduces the availability of clean water for other uses, such as agriculture and industry.

To address the issue of water pollution, the Foshan Water Supply and Drainage Bureau has implemented a series of measures. These include the construction of wastewater treatment plants and the enforcement of stricter regulations on industrial and domestic wastewater discharge.

The city's wastewater treatment plants aim to treat the city's wastewater to a high standard, making it suitable for reuse in agriculture and industry. These plants use a variety of treatment processes, including physical, chemical, and biological processes, to remove pollutants from the wastewater. The treated water is then either discharged into the Pearl River or reused within the city.

In addition to the treatment of wastewater, the city also enforces stricter regulations on industrial and domestic wastewater discharge. These regulations aim to limit the amount of pollutants that can be discharged into the city's water resources. They also require industries to treat their wastewater before discharging it.

Despite these efforts, water pollution remains a significant issue in Foshan. The city's rapid development and industrialization continue to put pressure on its water resources, and the pollution of the Pearl River persists. Therefore, it is crucial for the city to continue to invest in and improve its water pollution control measures.

In the next section, we will explore the role of water pollution control in Foshan's water resource management and discuss potential strategies for addressing this issue.

#### 9.2b Water Treatment and Purification in Foshan

Water treatment and purification are essential processes in Foshan's water resource management. These processes aim to remove pollutants from the city's water resources, making it safe for drinking and other uses.

The city's water treatment and purification processes are primarily carried out in its wastewater treatment plants. These plants use a variety of treatment processes, including physical, chemical, and biological processes, to remove pollutants from the wastewater. The treated water is then either discharged into the Pearl River or reused within the city.

Physical processes, such as sedimentation and filtration, are used to remove solid particles from the wastewater. Chemical processes, such as coagulation and flocculation, are used to remove dissolved substances from the water. Biological processes, such as activated sludge and trickling filters, are used to remove organic matter from the water.

In addition to these treatment processes, the city also enforces stricter regulations on industrial and domestic wastewater discharge. These regulations aim to limit the amount of pollutants that can be discharged into the city's water resources. They also require industries to treat their wastewater before discharging it.

Despite these efforts, water pollution remains a significant issue in Foshan. The city's rapid development and industrialization continue to put pressure on its water resources, and the pollution of the Pearl River persists. Therefore, it is crucial for the city to continue to invest in and improve its water treatment and purification processes.

In the next section, we will explore the role of water treatment and purification in Foshan's water resource management and discuss potential strategies for addressing this issue.

#### 9.2c Case Studies of Water Pollution Control in Foshan

Foshan's water pollution control efforts have been implemented through a variety of strategies, including the construction of wastewater treatment plants, the enforcement of stricter regulations on industrial and domestic wastewater discharge, and the implementation of advanced water treatment technologies. In this section, we will explore some case studies that highlight these efforts.

##### Case Study 1: Wastewater Treatment Plant Construction

The construction of wastewater treatment plants has been a key strategy in Foshan's water pollution control efforts. These plants use a variety of treatment processes, including physical, chemical, and biological processes, to remove pollutants from the city's water resources.

For example, the Shunde Wastewater Treatment Plant, located in the Shunde District of Foshan, is one of the city's largest wastewater treatment facilities. The plant has a treatment capacity of 200,000 cubic meters per day and uses a combination of physical, chemical, and biological processes to treat the city's wastewater. The plant's advanced treatment processes have significantly improved the quality of the city's water resources.

##### Case Study 2: Stricter Regulations on Industrial and Domestic Wastewater Discharge

Stricter regulations on industrial and domestic wastewater discharge have been another important strategy in Foshan's water pollution control efforts. These regulations aim to limit the amount of pollutants that can be discharged into the city's water resources and require industries to treat their wastewater before discharging it.

For instance, the Foshan Environmental Protection Bureau has implemented a series of regulations that limit the discharge of pollutants into the city's water resources. These regulations include limits on the concentration of pollutants that can be discharged, as well as requirements for industries to obtain permits before discharging wastewater. These regulations have been effective in reducing the amount of pollutants discharged into the city's water resources.

##### Case Study 3: Advanced Water Treatment Technologies

The implementation of advanced water treatment technologies has also been a key strategy in Foshan's water pollution control efforts. These technologies have been used to treat the city's wastewater to a high standard, making it suitable for reuse in agriculture and industry.

For example, the Foshan Water Supply and Drainage Bureau has implemented a series of advanced water treatment technologies, including membrane filtration and advanced oxidation processes. These technologies have been used to remove a wide range of pollutants from the city's wastewater, including heavy metals, organic matter, and microorganisms. The use of these technologies has significantly improved the quality of the city's water resources.

In conclusion, Foshan's water pollution control efforts have been implemented through a variety of strategies, including the construction of wastewater treatment plants, the enforcement of stricter regulations on industrial and domestic wastewater discharge, and the implementation of advanced water treatment technologies. These efforts have been effective in improving the quality of the city's water resources, but ongoing efforts will be necessary to address the ongoing challenges of water pollution in the city.




### Subsection: 9.1b Challenges and Issues in Water Resource Management

Foshan, like many other cities in China, faces significant challenges in managing its water resources. The city's rapid development and urbanization have put immense pressure on its water resources, leading to over-extraction of groundwater and falling water tables. This has resulted in serious land subsidence and flooding, further exacerbating the city's water scarcity.

#### 9.1b.1 Over-extraction of Groundwater

Over-extraction of groundwater is a major challenge in Foshan. The city's rapid development and urbanization have led to a significant increase in water demand, which has been met primarily through the extraction of groundwater. This has resulted in falling water tables and serious land subsidence, particularly in the northern part of the city. The over-extraction of groundwater has also led to a decrease in the quality of groundwater, as deeper wells reach the second and third layers of water, which are more prone to contamination from industrial and agricultural runoff.

#### 9.1b.2 Flooding and Land Subsidence

The over-extraction of groundwater has also led to flooding and land subsidence in Foshan. As the water table falls, the pressure on the ground decreases, leading to land subsidence. This has resulted in the sinking of the land surface, which can cause flooding during heavy rainfall or typhoons. The flooding not only poses a threat to human life and property but also exacerbates the city's water scarcity, as the flooded areas are unable to use the water for irrigation or other purposes.

#### 9.1b.3 Water Pollution

Water pollution is another major challenge in Foshan. The city's rapid industrialization and urbanization have led to the discharge of large amounts of pollutants into the city's water bodies, including the Pearl River. This has resulted in the deterioration of water quality and has made the water unsuitable for drinking and other purposes. The pollution of the Pearl River has also had a significant impact on the city's economy, as it is a major source of freshwater for the city.

#### 9.1b.4 Incomplete Legal and Regulatory Framework

The Second National Water Resources Meeting held in Buenos Aires in 2004 identified an incomplete and outdated legal and regulatory framework as a significant challenge in water management in Argentina. Similarly, in Foshan, the city's water management policies and regulations are incomplete and outdated, making it difficult to address the city's water challenges effectively. This is further exacerbated by the limited capacity of water management agencies at the central and provincial levels.

#### 9.1b.5 Lack of Integrated National Water Resources Information System and Deficient Water Resources Monitoring Network

The Second National Water Resources Meeting also identified the lack of an integrated national water resources information system and deficient water resources monitoring network as significant challenges in Argentina. In Foshan, the city's water resources are managed based on limited and outdated data, making it difficult to make informed decisions about water management. This is further exacerbated by the lack of a comprehensive water resources monitoring network, which makes it difficult to track changes in water resources and identify potential issues in a timely manner.

#### 9.1b.6 High Risk for Flooding in Urban and Rural Areas

The high risk for flooding in urban and rural areas is another significant challenge in Foshan. The city's rapid urbanization and development have led to the construction of buildings and infrastructure in areas prone to flooding, increasing the risk of flooding during heavy rainfall or typhoons. This not only poses a threat to human life and property but also exacerbates the city's water scarcity, as the flooded areas are unable to use the water for irrigation or other purposes.

#### 9.1b.7 Lack of Appropriate Incentives for Conservation and Efficient Use of the Resource Base and for Reducing Pollution

The Second National Water Resources Meeting also identified the lack of appropriate incentives for conservation and efficient use of the resource base and for reducing pollution as significant challenges in Argentina. In Foshan, the city's water management policies and regulations do not provide adequate incentives for conservation and efficient use of water resources, nor do they adequately address pollution. This has led to the over-extraction of groundwater, pollution of water bodies, and other water management challenges in the city.




### Subsection: 9.2a Water Conservation Measures

Water conservation is a critical aspect of sustainable water management in Foshan. It involves the efficient use of water resources to meet the city's needs while ensuring that these resources are not depleted or degraded. This section will discuss various water conservation measures that can be implemented in Foshan.

#### 9.2a.1 Water Use Efficiency

Water use efficiency refers to the amount of water used to produce a unit of output. In Foshan, improving water use efficiency can be achieved through various means, including the use of water-efficient technologies and practices. For instance, the use of low-flush toilets and high-efficiency washing machines can significantly reduce indoor water use. Similarly, the use of water-efficient irrigation systems can reduce outdoor water use.

#### 9.2a.2 Water Reuse and Recycling

Water reuse and recycling involve the use of treated wastewater for non-potable purposes. This can significantly reduce the demand for fresh water and help conserve the city's water resources. For instance, treated wastewater can be used for irrigation, industrial processes, and toilet flushing. In Foshan, the San Diego County Water Authority (SDCWA) has implemented various water reuse and recycling programs, including the Pure Water San Diego program, which aims to increase the use of recycled water to 20% by 2020.

#### 9.2a.3 Rainwater Harvesting

Rainwater harvesting involves the collection and storage of rainwater for later use. This can be particularly beneficial in Foshan, where heavy rainfall is common. Rainwater can be used for non-potable purposes such as irrigation, toilet flushing, and industrial processes. The SDCWA has implemented a rain barrel program to encourage residents to collect and use rainwater.

#### 9.2a.4 Water Pricing and Incentives

Water pricing and incentives can be used to encourage water conservation. By implementing a system of increasing block tariffs, where the price of water increases with consumption, residents and businesses are incentivized to use water more efficiently. Similarly, incentives can be provided for the installation of water-efficient technologies and practices. The SDCWA has implemented various water saving incentive programs for both residential and commercial consumers, including rebates for high-efficiency washers and toilets, and incentives for water-efficient landscaping.

#### 9.2a.5 Public Education and Awareness

Public education and awareness are crucial for promoting water conservation. By educating residents and businesses about the importance of water conservation and the benefits of water-efficient practices, the city can encourage a culture of water conservation. The SDCWA has implemented various public education programs, including water saving tips and gardening demonstrations, to promote water conservation among residents.

In conclusion, water conservation measures are essential for sustainable water management in Foshan. By implementing these measures, the city can ensure the efficient use of its water resources and help conserve these resources for future generations.




### Subsection: 9.2b Water Treatment and Purification

Water treatment and purification are crucial steps in the process of providing safe and clean water to the residents of Foshan. This section will discuss the various methods and technologies used for water treatment and purification in Foshan.

#### 9.2b.1 Water Treatment

Water treatment involves the removal of impurities and contaminants from water to make it safe for consumption and use. The treatment process typically involves several steps, including coagulation and flocculation, sedimentation, filtration, and disinfection.

##### Coagulation and Flocculation

Coagulation and flocculation are the first steps in the water treatment process. Coagulants, such as aluminum sulfate or ferric chloride, are added to the water to neutralize the negative charges of particles and allow them to clump together. Flocculants, such as polyacrylamide, are then added to form larger flocs that can be easily removed.

##### Sedimentation

During sedimentation, the water is allowed to settle undisturbed, allowing the flocs to settle at the bottom of the treatment tank. This process can take several hours.

##### Filtration

The water is then passed through filters to remove any remaining particles. The type of filter used depends on the quality of the source water. For instance, activated carbon filters can be used to remove organic compounds and improve taste and odor.

##### Disinfection

Finally, the water is disinfected to kill any remaining bacteria, viruses, and other microorganisms. Common disinfectants include chlorine, chloramine, and ultraviolet light.

#### 9.2b.2 Water Purification

Water purification is the process of removing dissolved impurities from water. This is typically achieved through reverse osmosis (RO), a process that uses a semipermeable membrane to remove ions, unwanted molecules, and larger particles from drinking water.

##### Reverse Osmosis

Reverse osmosis is a process that uses pressure to force water through a semipermeable membrane. The membrane is designed to allow water molecules to pass through, while blocking the passage of ions and other impurities. The process is energy-intensive and requires regular maintenance to prevent membrane fouling.

##### Ultraviolet Light (UV)

UV light is a powerful disinfectant that can kill bacteria, viruses, and other microorganisms. UV light is often used in conjunction with other treatment methods, such as filtration and disinfection, to provide safe and clean water.

##### Electrochemically Activated Solutions

Electrochemically activated solutions are a less common approach to water treatment. This method involves applying a current to water that has a small salt solution added to disinfect biological contaminants. Combined with filtration, this is a means to provide safe drinking water.

##### Desalination

Desalination is the process of removing salt and other impurities from seawater or brackish water to make it suitable for consumption. This process is particularly important in coastal communities where freshwater resources are scarce.

##### Water Softening

Water softening is a process that involves the addition of sodium and potassium ions to hard water to precipitate the hard minerals. This process can help prevent clogging of pipes and improve the effectiveness of soaps and detergents.




### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex and crucial topic of water resource management in Foshan, China. We have delved into the various challenges and opportunities that come with managing water resources in a rapidly developing urban area. From the historical context of water management in Foshan to the current state of water resources, we have examined the factors that have shaped the current situation and the potential solutions that can be implemented to address the challenges faced by the city.

We have also discussed the importance of a comprehensive and integrated approach to water resource management. This approach recognizes the interconnectedness of water resources and the need for coordinated management of all aspects of the water cycle, from supply and demand to pollution and conservation. It also emphasizes the importance of stakeholder participation and community involvement in decision-making processes.

Furthermore, we have highlighted the role of technology and innovation in water resource management. From advanced water treatment technologies to smart water management systems, technology has the potential to revolutionize the way water resources are managed in Foshan. However, it is crucial to ensure that these technologies are accessible and affordable to all members of the community, especially the most vulnerable and marginalized groups.

In conclusion, water resource management in Foshan is a complex and multifaceted issue that requires a comprehensive and integrated approach. It is essential to address the challenges faced by the city and to implement sustainable solutions that consider the needs and aspirations of all members of the community. By doing so, we can ensure the availability and sustainable management of water and sanitation for all in Foshan.

## Chapter 10: Urban Planning and Development:




### Introduction

In this chapter, we will explore the best practices and case studies in the field of urban planning and development. As we have seen throughout this book, Foshan, China has been a prime example of successful urban planning and development. In this chapter, we will delve deeper into the specific strategies and techniques that have been employed in Foshan, and how they can be applied to other cities around the world.
